Beyond Content Safety: Real-Time Monitoring for Reasoning Vulnerabilities in Large Language Models
Authors: Xunguang Wang, Yuguang Zhou, Qingyue Wang, Zongjie Li, Ruixuan Huang, Zhenlan Ji, Pingchuan Ma, Shuai Wang
First: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) increasingly rely on explicit chain-of-thought (CoT) reasoning to solve complex tasks, yet the safety of the reasoning process itself remains largely unaddressed. Existing work on LLM safety focuses on content safety--detecting harmful, biased, or factually incorrect outputs -- and treats the reasoning chain as an opaque intermediate artifact. We identify reasoning safety as an orthogonal and equally critical security dimension: the requirement that a model's reasoning trajectory be logically consistent, computationally efficient, and resistant to adversarial manipulation. We make three contributions. First, we formally define reasoning safety and introduce a nine-category taxonomy of unsafe reasoning behaviors, covering input parsing errors, reasoning execution errors, and process management errors. Second, we conduct a large-scale prevalence study annotating 4111 reasoning chains from both natural reasoning benchmarks and four adversarial attack methods (reasoning hijacking and denial-of-service), confirming that all nine error types occur in practice and that each attack induces a mechanistically interpretable signature. Third, we propose a Reasoning Safety Monitor: an external LLM-based component that runs in parallel with the target model, inspects each reasoning step in real time via a taxonomy-embedded prompt, and dispatches an interrupt signal upon detecting unsafe behavior. Evaluation on a 450-chain static benchmark shows that our monitor achieves up to 84.88\% step-level localization accuracy and 85.37\% error-type classification accuracy, outperforming hallucination detectors and process reward model baselines by substantial margins. These results demonstrate that reasoning-level monitoring is both necessary and practically achievable, and establish reasoning safety as a foundational concern for the secure deployment of large reasoning models.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越内容安全：大型语言模型推理漏洞的实时监控
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越依赖显式的思维链（CoT）推理来解决复杂任务，但推理过程本身的安全性仍然在很大程度上未得到解决。现有的LLM安全工作集中于内容安全——检测有害、偏见或事实不准确的输出——并将推理链视为不透明的中间产物。我们将推理安全识别为一个正交且同样重要的安全维度：模型的推理轨迹必须在逻辑上保持一致、计算上高效，并且抵御对抗性操控。我们做出了三项贡献。首先，我们正式定义了推理安全，并引入了一个涵盖输入解析错误、推理执行错误和过程管理错误的九类不安全推理行为的分类法。其次，我们进行了一项大规模的流行度研究，注释了来自自然推理基准和四种对抗攻击方法（推理劫持和拒绝服务）的4111条推理链，确认所有九种错误类型在实践中确实存在，并且每种攻击都会产生可机械解释的特征。第三，我们提出了推理安全监控器：一个基于LLM的外部组件，与目标模型并行运行，通过嵌入分类法的提示实时检查每个推理步骤，并在检测到不安全行为时发出中断信号。在450条链的静态基准测试中的评估显示，我们的监控器在步骤级定位准确率上达到84.88%和错误类型分类准确率达到85.37%，显著优于幻觉检测器和过程奖励模型基线。这些结果表明，推理级监控既是必要的，也是可实际实现的，并确立了推理安全作为大型推理模型安全部署的基础性关注点。

The research addresses the overlooked aspect of reasoning safety in large language models (LLMs), which is critical for ensuring that the reasoning process is logically consistent and resistant to adversarial manipulation. Previous methods primarily focused on content safety, failing to consider the reasoning chain as a significant factor in model safety. This paper proposes a novel approach by defining reasoning safety and introducing a taxonomy of unsafe reasoning behaviors, along with a Reasoning Safety Monitor that evaluates reasoning steps in real time. The methodology involves annotating a large dataset of reasoning chains and implementing the monitor, which demonstrated high accuracy in detecting unsafe behaviors. The results indicate that the proposed method significantly improves upon existing safety measures, highlighting the importance of reasoning safety in the deployment of LLMs.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）中被忽视的推理安全性，这对于确保其推理过程的逻辑一致性和计算效率至关重要。以往的方法主要集中在内容安全上，检测有害输出，同时将推理视为一个不透明的过程，导致对推理漏洞的理解存在缺口。本文提出了一种新方法，通过定义推理安全性并引入不安全推理行为的分类法，以及一个实时评估推理步骤的推理安全监控器。该方法包括对推理链的大规模研究，揭示了各种推理错误的普遍性和所提监控器的有效性，该监控器在基准测试中实现了高达84.88%的定位准确率和85.37%的错误类型分类准确率，从而支持了在大型语言模型安全部署中进行推理级监控的必要性。
Enhancing Jailbreak Attacks on LLMs via Persona Prompts
Authors: Zheng Zhang, Peilin Zhao, Deheng Ye, Hao Wang
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2025-07-28T12:03:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-25T15:46:17+00:00
Comments: Workshop on LLM Persona Modeling at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Jailbreak attacks aim to exploit large language models (LLMs) by inducing them to generate harmful content, thereby revealing their vulnerabilities. Understanding and addressing these attacks is crucial for advancing the field of LLM safety. Previous jailbreak approaches have mainly focused on direct manipulations of harmful intent, with limited attention to the impact of persona prompts. In this study, we systematically explore the efficacy of persona prompts in compromising LLM defenses. We propose a genetic algorithm-based method that automatically crafts persona prompts to bypass LLM's safety mechanisms. Our experiments reveal that: (1) our evolved persona prompts reduce refusal rates by 50-70% across multiple LLMs, and (2) these prompts demonstrate synergistic effects when combined with existing attack methods, increasing success rates by 10-20%. Our code and data are available at https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过角色提示增强对大型语言模型的越狱攻击
越狱攻击旨在利用大型语言模型（LLMs），诱使其生成有害内容，从而揭示其脆弱性。理解和应对这些攻击对推动LLM安全领域至关重要。以往的越狱方法主要集中在对有害意图的直接操控上，而对角色提示的影响关注较少。在本研究中，我们系统地探讨了角色提示在破坏LLM防御中的有效性。我们提出了一种基于遗传算法的方法，自动生成角色提示以绕过LLM的安全机制。我们的实验表明：（1）我们演化的角色提示在多个LLM中将拒绝率降低了50-70%；（2）这些提示与现有攻击方法结合时表现出协同效应，成功率提高了10-20%。我们的代码和数据可在https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona获取。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the vulnerabilities of large language models (LLMs) to jailbreak attacks, which exploit these models to generate harmful content. Previous methods primarily focused on direct manipulations of harmful intent, neglecting the role of persona prompts, which this study identifies as a significant factor in LLM defenses. The proposed approach utilizes a genetic algorithm to automatically generate persona prompts that effectively bypass safety mechanisms, thereby enhancing the attack's efficacy. This methodology is well-motivated by the need to improve LLM safety. The experiments demonstrate that the evolved persona prompts can reduce refusal rates by 50-70% across various LLMs and, when combined with existing attack strategies, can increase success rates by 10-20%, thus supporting the research goals of advancing LLM safety measures.
本文探讨了针对大型语言模型（LLMs）的越狱攻击日益严重的问题，这些攻击利用这些系统生成有害内容并暴露其脆弱性。以往的方法主要集中在直接操控有害意图上，往往忽视了角色提示的作用，而本研究则将其视为LLM防御中的一个重要因素。所提出的方法利用遗传算法自动生成角色提示，有效绕过安全机制，从而解决了早期方法的局限性。该研究的贡献在于证明进化的角色提示可以显著降低多种LLM的拒绝率50-70%，并通过提高现有攻击策略的成功率10-20%来增强其有效性。这种方法展示了一种新颖的方式来破坏LLM防御，支持了推进LLM安全研究的目标。
SafeSeek: Universal Attribution of Safety Circuits in Language Models
Authors: Miao Yu, Siyuan Fu, Moayad Aloqaily, Zhenhong Zhou, Safa Otoum, Xing fan, Kun Wang, Yufei Guo, Qingsong Wen
First: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Mechanistic interpretability reveals that safety-critical behaviors (e.g., alignment, jailbreak, backdoor) in Large Language Models (LLMs) are grounded in specialized functional components. However, existing safety attribution methods struggle with generalization and reliability due to their reliance on heuristic, domain-specific metrics and search algorithms. To address this, we propose \ourmethod, a unified safety interpretability framework that identifies functionally complete safety circuits in LLMs via optimization. Unlike methods focusing on isolated heads or neurons, \ourmethod introduces differentiable binary masks to extract multi-granular circuits through gradient descent on safety datasets, while integrates Safety Circuit Tuning to utilize these sparse circuits for efficient safety fine-tuning. We validate \ourmethod in two key scenarios in LLM safety: \textbf{(1) backdoor attacks}, identifying a backdoor circuit with 0.42\% sparsity, whose ablation eradicates the Attack Success Rate (ASR) from 100\% $\to$ 0.4\% while retaining over 99\% general utility; \textbf{(2) safety alignment}, localizing an alignment circuit with 3.03\% heads and 0.79\% neurons, whose removal spikes ASR from 0.8\% $\to$ 96.9\%, whereas excluding this circuit during helpfulness fine-tuning maintains 96.5\% safety retention.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeSeek：语言模型中安全电路的通用归因
机械解释性揭示了大型语言模型（LLMs）中安全关键行为（例如，调整、越狱、后门）是基于专门的功能组件。然而，现有的安全归因方法由于依赖启发式、特定领域的指标和搜索算法，难以实现泛化和可靠性。为了解决这个问题，我们提出了\ourmethod，一个统一的安全解释框架，通过优化识别LLMs中的功能完整安全电路。与专注于孤立头部或神经元的方法不同，\ourmethod引入可微分的二进制掩码，通过对安全数据集的梯度下降提取多粒度电路，同时集成安全电路调优，以利用这些稀疏电路进行高效的安全微调。我们在LLM安全的两个关键场景中验证了\ourmethod：\textbf{(1) 后门攻击}，识别出一个稀疏度为0.42\%的后门电路，其消融使攻击成功率（ASR）从100\%降至0.4\%，同时保留超过99\%的通用效用；\textbf{(2) 安全对齐}，定位一个稀疏度为3.03\%的对齐电路和0.79\%的神经元，其移除使ASR从0.8\%激增至96.9\%，而在有用性微调中排除该电路则保持96.5\%的安全保留。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of ensuring safety in Large Language Models (LLMs), where existing safety attribution methods are limited by their reliance on heuristic and domain-specific metrics, leading to issues with generalization and reliability. The proposed method, SafeSeek, differs by introducing a unified safety interpretability framework that employs differentiable binary masks to identify functionally complete safety circuits through optimization, rather than focusing on isolated components. This approach is well-motivated as it enhances the understanding and fine-tuning of safety mechanisms in LLMs. The methodology includes the identification of safety circuits using gradient descent on safety datasets and incorporates Safety Circuit Tuning for efficient fine-tuning. The experiments demonstrate that SafeSeek effectively identifies a backdoor circuit with 0.42% sparsity, significantly reducing the Attack Success Rate from 100% to 0.4%, and localizes an alignment circuit that, when removed, increases the Attack Success Rate from 0.8% to 96.9%, while maintaining high safety retention during helpfulness fine-tuning.
本研究解决了大型语言模型（LLMs）安全性的问题，现有的安全归因方法由于依赖启发式和领域特定的指标，往往缺乏泛化能力和可靠性。所提出的方法SafeSeek与过去的方法不同，它利用统一的安全可解释性框架，通过优化识别功能完整的安全电路，而不是关注孤立的组件。该方法的动机明确，因为它引入了可微分的二进制掩码，通过梯度下降提取多层次电路，并结合安全电路调优以实现高效的安全微调。论文的贡献通过两个场景得到了验证：它成功识别出一个稀疏性极低的后门电路，显著降低了攻击成功率，同时保持了通用性；并且定位了一个对齐电路，其移除显著提高了攻击成功率，证明了所提出的方法在增强LLM安全性方面的有效性。
DriveSafe: A Hierarchical Risk Taxonomy for Safety-Critical LLM-Based Driving Assistants
Authors: Abhishek Kumar, Riya Tapwal, Carsten Maple
First: 2026-01-17T18:50:47+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-23T18:19:05+00:00
Comments: This is the revised version of the paper
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) are increasingly integrated into vehicle-based digital assistants, where unsafe, ambiguous, or legally incorrect responses can lead to serious safety, ethical, and regulatory consequences. Despite growing interest in LLM safety, existing taxonomies and evaluation frameworks remain largely general-purpose and fail to capture the domain-specific risks inherent to real-world driving scenarios. In this paper, we introduce DriveSafe, a hierarchical, four-level risk taxonomy designed to systematically characterize safety-critical failure modes of LLM-based driving assistants. The taxonomy comprises 129 fine-grained atomic risk categories spanning technical, legal, societal, and ethical dimensions, grounded in real-world driving regulations and safety principles and reviewed by domain experts. To validate the safety relevance and realism of the constructed prompts, we evaluate their refusal behavior across six widely deployed LLMs. Our analysis shows that the evaluated models often fail to appropriately refuse unsafe or non-compliant driving-related queries, underscoring the limitations of general-purpose safety alignment in driving contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：DriveSafe：安全关键型基于LLM的驾驶助手的分层风险分类法
大型语言模型（LLM）越来越多地集成到基于车辆的数字助手中，其中不安全、模糊或法律上不正确的响应可能导致严重的安全、伦理和监管后果。尽管对LLM安全性的关注日益增加，但现有的分类法和评估框架仍然主要是通用的，未能捕捉到现实驾驶场景中固有的特定领域风险。本文介绍了DriveSafe，一种分层的四级风险分类法，旨在系统地描述基于LLM的驾驶助手的安全关键型故障模式。该分类法包括129个细粒度的原子风险类别，涵盖技术、法律、社会和伦理维度，基于现实世界的驾驶法规和安全原则，并经过领域专家的审查。为了验证构建的提示的安全相关性和现实性，我们评估了六个广泛部署的LLM的拒绝行为。我们的分析表明，被评估的模型往往未能适当地拒绝不安全或不合规的驾驶相关查询，突显了在驾驶环境中通用安全对齐的局限性。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the increasing integration of Large Language Models (LLMs) in vehicle-based digital assistants, highlighting the potential safety, ethical, and regulatory risks associated with unsafe or ambiguous responses. Previous methods have relied on general-purpose taxonomies and evaluation frameworks, which do not adequately capture the specific risks related to driving scenarios. The proposed approach, DriveSafe, introduces a hierarchical four-level risk taxonomy that includes 129 detailed risk categories focused on technical, legal, societal, and ethical aspects, thus providing a more relevant framework for assessing LLM safety in driving contexts. The methodology involves evaluating the refusal behavior of six widely used LLMs against the constructed prompts to ensure safety relevance. The findings reveal that these models frequently fail to refuse unsafe or non-compliant driving-related queries, demonstrating the inadequacy of existing safety alignment approaches in this critical application area.

Using LLM-as-a-Judge/Jury to Advance Scalable, Clinically-Validated Safety Evaluations of Model Responses to Users Demonstrating Psychosis
Authors: May Lynn Reese, Markela Zeneli, Mindy Ng, Jacob Haimes, Andreea Damien, Elizabeth Stade
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00
Comments: published at IASEAI 2026, preliminary work presented at GenAI4Health workshop at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
General-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) are becoming widely adopted by people for mental health support. Yet emerging evidence suggests there are significant risks associated with high-frequency use, particularly for individuals suffering from psychosis, as LLMs may reinforce delusions and hallucinations. Existing evaluations of LLMs in mental health contexts are limited by a lack of clinical validation and scalability of assessment. To address these issues, this research focuses on psychosis as a critical condition for LLM safety evaluation by (1) developing and validating seven clinician-informed safety criteria, (2) constructing a human-consensus dataset, and (3) testing automated assessment using an LLM as an evaluator (LLM-as-a-Judge) or taking the majority vote of several LLM judges (LLM-as-a-Jury). Results indicate that LLM-as-a-Judge aligns closely with the human consensus (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$) and that the best judge slightly outperforms LLM-as-a-Jury (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$). Overall, these findings have promising implications for clinically grounded, scalable methods in LLM safety evaluations for mental health contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：使用LLM作为评判者/陪审团推进可扩展的临床验证模型响应用户精神病的安全评估
通用大型语言模型（LLMs）正被广泛应用于心理健康支持。然而， emerging evidence表明，高频使用存在显著风险，尤其是对精神病患者，因为LLMs可能会强化妄想和幻觉。现有的LLMs在心理健康背景下的评估受限于缺乏临床验证和评估的可扩展性。为了解决这些问题，本研究将精神病作为LLM安全评估的关键条件，(1) 开发和验证七个临床知情的安全标准，(2) 构建人类共识数据集，以及(3) 使用LLM作为评估者（LLM作为评判者）或采取多个LLM评判者的多数投票（LLM作为陪审团）进行自动评估。结果表明，LLM作为评判者与人类共识高度一致（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$），而最佳评判者略微优于LLM作为陪审团（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$）。总体而言，这些发现对心理健康背景下LLM安全评估的临床基础、可扩展方法具有良好的启示。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing concern regarding the safety of general-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) in mental health support, particularly for individuals with psychosis, as existing evaluations lack clinical validation and scalability. Previous methods have not adequately assessed the risks associated with LLM use in this context, leading to potential reinforcement of delusions and hallucinations. This study proposes a novel approach by developing seven clinician-informed safety criteria, creating a human-consensus dataset, and utilizing LLMs as evaluators (LLM-as-a-Judge) or in a majority voting system (LLM-as-a-Jury) to enhance safety evaluations. The methodology demonstrates that LLM-as-a-Judge closely aligns with human consensus, achieving Cohen's kappa values indicating strong agreement, and slightly outperforms the LLM-as-a-Jury approach. These findings contribute to the development of clinically validated and scalable safety evaluation methods for LLMs in mental health applications, supporting the need for rigorous assessments in this domain.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）在心理健康支持中的日益使用，特别强调它们对精神病患者可能造成的风险，例如加重妄想和幻觉。以往对LLMs的评估缺乏临床验证和可扩展性，本研究旨在通过开发七项临床医生知情的安全标准、创建人类共识数据集，并采用LLM作为评估者（LLM-as-a-Judge）或使用多个LLM进行多数投票（LLM-as-a-Jury）来克服这些问题。本文的贡献在于提出了一种新的框架，用于评估心理健康背景下LLM的安全性，结果表明LLM-as-a-Judge与人类共识高度一致，并且略微优于LLM-as-a-Jury方法。该方法在评估LLM响应方面显示出良好的结果，达成了支持可扩展和临床验证的安全评估目标的高一致性得分。
LISAA: A Framework for Large Language Model Information Security Awareness Assessment
Authors: Ofir Cohen, Gil Ari Agmon, Asaf Shabtai, Rami Puzis
First: 2024-11-20T11:09:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-19T22:34:14+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The popularity of large language models (LLMs) continues to grow, and LLM-based assistants have become ubiquitous. Information security awareness (ISA) is an important yet underexplored area of LLM safety. ISA encompasses LLMs' security knowledge, which has been explored in the past, as well as their attitudes and behaviors, which are crucial to LLMs' ability to understand implicit security context and reject unsafe requests that may cause an LLM to unintentionally fail the user. We introduce LISAA, a comprehensive framework to assess LLM ISA. The proposed framework applies an automated measurement method to a comprehensive set of 100 realistic scenarios covering all security topics in an ISA taxonomy. These scenarios create tension between implicit security implications and user satisfaction. Applying our LISAA framework to leading LLMs highlights a widespread vulnerability affecting current deployments: many popular models exhibit only medium to low ISA levels, exposing their users to cybersecurity threats, and models that rank highly in cybersecurity knowledge benchmarks sometimes achieve relatively low ISA ranking. In addition, we found that smaller variants of the same model family are significantly riskier. Furthermore, while newer model versions demonstrated notable improvements, meaningful gaps in their ISA persist, suggesting that there is room for improvement. We release an online tool that implements our framework and enables the evaluation of new models.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LISAA：大型语言模型信息安全意识评估框架
大型语言模型（LLMs）的普及持续增长，基于LLM的助手已变得无处不在。信息安全意识（ISA）是LLM安全性的重要但尚未充分探索的领域。ISA包括LLM的安全知识，这在过去已有研究，以及它们的态度和行为，这对LLM理解隐含安全上下文和拒绝可能导致LLM无意中未能满足用户的安全请求至关重要。我们介绍了LISAA，一个全面评估LLM ISA的框架。该框架采用自动测量方法，涵盖ISA分类法中所有安全主题的100个现实场景。这些场景在隐含安全含义和用户满意度之间产生紧张关系。将我们的LISAA框架应用于领先的LLM，突显了当前部署中普遍存在的脆弱性：许多流行模型的ISA水平仅为中等到低，暴露其用户于网络安全威胁中，而在网络安全知识基准中排名较高的模型有时在ISA排名中相对较低。此外，我们发现同一模型家族的小型变体风险显著更高。此外，尽管较新版本的模型表现出显著改善，但它们的ISA仍存在显著差距，表明仍有改进空间。我们发布了一个在线工具，实施我们的框架并支持新模型的评估。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing importance of information security awareness (ISA) in the context of large language models (LLMs), which have become widely used but often lack adequate security knowledge and behaviors. Previous methods have primarily focused on LLMs' security knowledge without adequately assessing their attitudes and behaviors, leading to vulnerabilities in their ability to handle implicit security contexts. The proposed LISAA framework differs by providing a comprehensive assessment of ISA through automated measurements across 100 realistic scenarios that balance security implications with user satisfaction. This framework reveals that many leading LLMs exhibit only medium to low ISA levels, exposing users to cybersecurity threats, and highlights that smaller model variants pose greater risks. The study demonstrates that while newer model versions show improvements, significant gaps in ISA remain, indicating further enhancement is necessary. The framework is implemented in an online tool for evaluating new models, contributing to the field by addressing a critical gap in LLM safety assessment.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）中信息安全意识（ISA）日益重要性，尽管这些模型被广泛使用，但往往缺乏足够的安全知识和行为。以往的方法主要集中在LLMs的安全知识上，而忽视了其态度和行为，导致在处理隐含安全上下文时存在脆弱性。提出的LISAA框架通过自动化测量方法，对100个现实场景进行全面评估，平衡安全隐含与用户满意度，从而与现有方法有所不同。该框架揭示许多领先的LLMs仅表现出中等到低水平的ISA，暴露用户于网络安全威胁中，并强调较小模型变体的显著风险。研究方法表明，尽管较新模型显示出改进，但ISA仍存在显著差距，表明需要进一步提升。该研究通过提供一个在线工具来评估基于ISA的LLMs，为开发更安全的人工智能系统提供了支持。
IndicSafe: A Benchmark for Evaluating Multilingual LLM Safety in South Asia
Authors: Priyaranjan Pattnayak, Sanchari Chowdhuri
First: 2026-03-18T16:54:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-18T16:54:07+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) are deployed in multilingual settings, their safety behavior in culturally diverse, low-resource languages remains poorly understood. We present the first systematic evaluation of LLM safety across 12 Indic languages, spoken by over 1.2 billion people but underrepresented in LLM training data. Using a dataset of 6,000 culturally grounded prompts spanning caste, religion, gender, health, and politics, we assess 10 leading LLMs on translated variants of the prompt. Our analysis reveals significant safety drift: cross-language agreement is just 12.8\%, and \texttt{SAFE} rate variance exceeds 17\% across languages. Some models over-refuse benign prompts in low-resource scripts, overflag politically sensitive topics, while others fail to flag unsafe generations. We quantify these failures using prompt-level entropy, category bias scores, and multilingual consistency indices. Our findings highlight critical safety generalization gaps in multilingual LLMs and show that safety alignment does not transfer evenly across languages. We release \textsc{IndicSafe}, the first benchmark to enable culturally informed safety evaluation for Indic deployments, and advocate for language-aware alignment strategies grounded in regional harms.
中文标题/摘要
标题：IndicSafe：评估南亚多语言LLM安全性的基准
随着大型语言模型（LLMs）在多语言环境中的部署，它们在文化多样性和资源匮乏语言中的安全行为仍然不够了解。我们首次系统性地评估了12种印地语言的LLM安全性，这些语言由超过12亿人使用，但在LLM训练数据中代表性不足。使用涵盖种姓、宗教、性别、健康和政治的6000个文化背景提示的数据集，我们评估了10个领先的LLM在提示翻译变体上的表现。 我们的分析揭示了显著的安全漂移：跨语言一致性仅为12.8%，而安全率方差在不同语言间超过17%。一些模型在资源匮乏的脚本中过度拒绝良性提示，过度标记政治敏感话题，而其他模型则未能标记不安全的生成。我们使用提示级熵、类别偏差分数和多语言一致性指数量化这些失败。 我们的发现突显了多语言LLM中关键的安全泛化差距，并表明安全对齐在不同语言间并不均匀转移。我们发布了IndicSafe，这是第一个基准，旨在为印地语言的文化知情安全评估提供支持，并倡导基于区域危害的语言意识对齐策略。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the inadequate understanding of safety behaviors in large language models (LLMs) when deployed in multilingual settings, particularly in culturally diverse and low-resource languages of South Asia. Previous methods lacked systematic evaluation and often overlooked the unique cultural contexts of these languages, leading to significant safety gaps. The proposed approach introduces IndicSafe, a benchmark that evaluates LLM safety across 12 Indic languages using a dataset of 6,000 culturally relevant prompts. This methodology reveals substantial safety drift, with only 12.8% cross-language agreement and over 17% variance in safety rates, highlighting the need for language-aware alignment strategies. The findings underscore critical safety generalization gaps and provide a foundation for improving LLM safety in underrepresented languages, supporting the goal of culturally informed AI deployment.
本研究关注在多语言和文化多样化环境中，特别是在低资源的印度语言中，大型语言模型（LLMs）安全行为的不足理解。以往的方法未能系统性地评估这些语言中的LLM安全性，导致安全性能存在显著差距。提出的方法引入了IndicSafe，一个基准，系统评估10种领先的LLM在12种印度语言中的安全性，使用了6000个文化相关提示的数据集。该方法揭示了显著的安全漂移，跨语言一致性仅为12.8%，安全率的方差超过17%，表明安全对齐在语言间并不均匀转移。研究结果有助于理解多语言LLM中的安全泛化差距，并倡导进行文化知情的安全评估和语言意识的对齐策略。
Efficient LLM Safety Evaluation through Multi-Agent Debate
Authors: Dachuan Lin, Guobin Shen, Zihao Yang, Tianrong Liu, Dongcheng Zhao, Yi Zeng
First: 2025-11-09T14:06:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-18T02:09:28+00:00
Comments: 15 pages, 5 figures, 10 tables. Updated abstract to fix an incconsistency issue with the main paper: HAJailBench size (12,000 -> 11,100)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Safety evaluation of large language models (LLMs) increasingly relies on LLM-as-a-judge pipelines, but strong judges can still be expensive to use at scale. We study whether structured multi-agent debate can improve judge reliability while keeping backbone size and cost modest. To do so, we introduce HAJailBench, a human-annotated jailbreak benchmark with 11,100 labeled interactions spanning diverse attack methods and target models, and we pair it with a Multi-Agent Judge framework in which critic, defender, and judge agents debate under a shared safety rubric. On HAJailBench, the framework improves over matched small-model prompt baselines and prior multi-agent judges, while remaining more economical than GPT-4o under the evaluated pricing snapshot. Ablation results further show that a small number of debate rounds is sufficient to capture most of the gain. Together, these results support structured, value-aligned debate as a practical design for scalable LLM safety evaluation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过多智能体辩论进行高效的LLM安全评估
大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全评估越来越依赖于LLM作为评审的管道，但强大的评审在大规模使用时仍然成本高昂。我们研究结构化的多智能体辩论是否能在保持骨干规模和成本适中的同时提高评审的可靠性。为此，我们引入了HAJailBench，这是一个人类注释的越狱基准，包含11,100个标记的交互，涵盖多种攻击方法和目标模型，并将其与多智能体评审框架配对，在该框架中，批评者、辩护者和评审代理在共享的安全标准下进行辩论。在HAJailBench上，该框架在匹配的小模型提示基线和先前的多智能体评审中表现更好，同时在评估的定价快照下仍然比GPT-4o更经济。消融结果进一步表明，少量的辩论轮次足以捕捉到大部分增益。综合来看，这些结果支持结构化、价值对齐的辩论作为可扩展LLM安全评估的实用设计。
Summary / 总结

Previous methods have struggled with reliability and cost, prompting the authors to propose a structured multi-agent debate framework that includes critic, defender, and judge agents to enhance judge reliability while minimizing costs. The paper introduces HAJailBench, a benchmark with 11,100 labeled interactions, and demonstrates that their multi-agent debate framework outperforms existing small-model prompt baselines and prior multi-agent judges in terms of performance while being more economical than GPT-4o. SFCoT: Safer Chain-of-Thought via Active Safety Evaluation and Calibration
Authors: Yu Pan, Wenlong Yu, Tiejun Wu, Xiaohu Ye, Qiannan Si, Guangquan Xu, Bin Wu
First: 2026-03-16T15:13:21+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-16T15:13:21+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have demonstrated remarkable capabilities in complex reasoning tasks. However, they remain highly susceptible to jailbreak attacks that undermine their safety alignment. Existing defense mechanisms typically rely on post hoc filtering applied only to the final output, leaving intermediate reasoning steps unmonitored and vulnerable to adversarial manipulation. To address this gap, this paper proposes a SaFer Chain-of-Thought (SFCoT) framework, which proactively evaluates and calibrates potentially unsafe reasoning steps in real time. SFCoT incorporates a three-tier safety scoring system alongside a multi-perspective consistency verification mechanism, designed to detect potential risks throughout the reasoning process. A dynamic intervention module subsequently performs targeted calibration to redirect reasoning trajectories toward safe outcomes. Experimental results demonstrate that SFCoT reduces the attack success rate from $58.97\%$ to $12.31\%$, demonstrating it as an effective and efficient LLM safety enhancement method without a significant decline in general performance.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SFCoT：通过主动安全评估和校准实现更安全的思维链
大型语言模型（LLMs）在复杂推理任务中表现出显著能力。然而，它们仍然高度易受破坏攻击，影响其安全对齐。现有的防御机制通常依赖于仅应用于最终输出的事后过滤，导致中间推理步骤未被监控，易受对抗性操控。为了解决这一问题，本文提出了一种更安全的思维链（SFCoT）框架，能够实时主动评估和校准潜在不安全的推理步骤。SFCoT结合了三级安全评分系统和多角度一致性验证机制，旨在检测推理过程中的潜在风险。动态干预模块随后执行针对性校准，以将推理轨迹引导至安全结果。实验结果表明，SFCoT将攻击成功率从58.97%降低至12.31%，证明其作为一种有效且高效的LLM安全增强方法，且未显著降低整体性能。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the vulnerability of large language models (LLMs) to jailbreak attacks that compromise their safety alignment, highlighting the inadequacy of existing defense mechanisms that only filter final outputs without monitoring intermediate reasoning steps. The proposed SaFer Chain-of-Thought (SFCoT) framework differs from past methods by proactively evaluating and calibrating unsafe reasoning steps in real time, utilizing a three-tier safety scoring system and a multi-perspective consistency verification mechanism to identify risks throughout the reasoning process. The contribution of this paper lies in its innovative approach to enhancing LLM safety through dynamic intervention, which effectively redirects reasoning trajectories toward safer outcomes. The methodology involves real-time safety evaluations and targeted calibrations, and experimental results show that SFCoT significantly reduces the attack success rate from 58.97% to 12.31%, indicating its effectiveness in improving safety without compromising overall performance.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）在面临危害其安全对齐的越狱攻击时的脆弱性，强调现有防御机制仅对最终输出进行过滤，而未监控中间推理步骤的不足。所提出的安全链式思维（SFCoT）框架与过去的方法不同，它通过实时主动评估和校准潜在不安全的推理，利用三层安全评分系统和多角度一致性验证机制来识别推理过程中的风险。这种方法的动机明确，旨在在保持性能的同时增强LLMs的安全性。该方法论包括一个动态干预模块，重新校准推理轨迹以确保更安全的结果。实验结果表明，SFCoT将攻击成功率从58.97%显著降低到12.31%，表明其在提高LLM安全性方面的有效性，同时不影响整体性能。
From Evaluation to Defense: Advancing Safety in Video Large Language Models
Authors: Yiwei Sun, Peiqi Jiang, Chuanbin Liu, Luohao Lin, Zhiying Lu, Hongtao Xie
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-05-22T13:16:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-16T13:05:37+00:00
Comments: Accepted at ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
While the safety risks of image-based large language models (Image LLMs) have been extensively studied, their video-based counterparts (Video LLMs) remain critically under-examined. To systematically study this problem, we introduce VideoSafetyEval - a large-scale, real-world benchmark for Video LLM safety, which comprises 11.4k video-query pairs and spans 19 principal risk categories. Based on this, we reveal that integrating video modality degrades safety performance by an average of 34.2%, thereby exposing systemic risks in multimodal attack exploitation. To address this vulnerability, we propose VideoSafety-R1, a dual-stage framework achieving unprecedented safety gains through three innovations: (1) the VideoSafetyThinking dataset contains 46k video-query-thinking response triplets; (2) Alarm Token-Guided Safety Fine-Tuning (AT-SFT) injects learnable alarm tokens into visual and textual sequences, enabling explicit harm perception across modalities via multitask objectives; and (3) safety-guided GRPO enhances defensive reasoning through dynamic policy optimization with rule-based rewards derived from dual-modality verification. These components synergize to shift safety alignment from harm perception to active reasoning. The framework achieves a 71.1% improvement on VSE-HH, and improves by 59.1%, 44.3%, and 15.0% on the image safety datasets MMBench, VLGuard, and FigStep, respectively. Our code and dataset are available at https://github.com/Emiya-syw/VideoSafety-R1.git. Note: This paper contains harmful language and image examples, and reader discretion is recommended.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从评估到防御：提升视频大型语言模型的安全性
尽管基于图像的大型语言模型（图像LLM）的安全风险已被广泛研究，但其视频基础的对应模型（视频LLM）仍然缺乏深入的研究。为系统性地研究这个问题，我们引入了VideoSafetyEval——一个针对视频LLM安全性的大规模现实基准，包含11.4k个视频-查询对，涵盖19个主要风险类别。基于此，我们揭示了视频模态的整合使安全性能平均下降34.2%，从而暴露了多模态攻击利用中的系统性风险。为了解决这一脆弱性，我们提出了VideoSafety-R1，一个通过三项创新实现前所未有的安全提升的双阶段框架：（1）VideoSafetyThinking数据集包含46k个视频-查询-思考响应三元组；（2）报警令牌引导的安全微调（AT-SFT）将可学习的报警令牌注入视觉和文本序列，通过多任务目标实现跨模态的明确伤害感知；（3）安全引导的GRPO通过基于规则的奖励优化动态策略，增强防御推理。这些组件协同作用，将安全对齐从伤害感知转向主动推理。该框架在VSE-HH上实现了71.1%的提升，并在图像安全数据集MMBench、VLGuard和FigStep上分别提高了59.1%、44.3%和15.0%。我们的代码和数据集可在https://github.com/Emiya-syw/VideoSafety-R1.git获取。注意：本文包含有害语言和图像示例，建议读者谨慎阅读。

OffTopicEval: When Large Language Models Enter the Wrong Chat, Almost Always!
Authors: Jingdi Lei, Varun Gumma, Rishabh Bhardwaj, Seok Min Lim, Chuan Li, Amir Zadeh, Soujanya Poria
First: 2025-09-30T16:39:17+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-13T11:01:37+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Model (LLM) safety is one of the most pressing challenges for enabling wide-scale deployment. While most studies and global discussions focus on generic harms, such as models assisting users in harming themselves or others, enterprises face a more fundamental concern: whether LLM-based agents are safe for their intended use case. To address this, we introduce operational safety, defined as an LLM's ability to appropriately accept or refuse user queries when tasked with a specific purpose. We further propose OffTopicEval, an evaluation suite and benchmark for measuring operational safety both in general and within specific agentic use cases. Our evaluations on six model families comprising 20 open-weight LLMs reveal that while performance varies across models, all of them remain highly operationally unsafe. Even the strongest models - Qwen-3 (235B) with 77.77% and Mistral (24B) with 79.96% - fall far short of reliable operational safety, while GPT models plateau in the 62-73% range, Phi achieves only mid-level scores (48-70%), and Gemma and Llama-3 collapse to 39.53% and 23.84%, respectively. While operational safety is a core model alignment issue, to suppress these failures, we propose prompt-based steering methods: query grounding (Q-ground) and system-prompt grounding (P-ground), which substantially improve OOD refusal. Q-ground provides consistent gains of up to 23%, while P-ground delivers even larger boosts, raising Llama-3.3 (70B) by 41% and Qwen-3 (30B) by 27%. These results highlight both the urgent need for operational safety interventions and the promise of prompt-based steering as a first step toward more reliable LLM-based agents.
中文标题/摘要
标题：OffTopicEval：当大型语言模型进入错误的聊天时，几乎总是如此！
大型语言模型（LLM）安全性是实现大规模部署的最紧迫挑战之一。虽然大多数研究和全球讨论集中在一般性危害上，例如模型帮助用户伤害自己或他人，但企业面临更根本的担忧：基于LLM的代理是否安全用于其预期用途。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了操作安全性，定义为LLM在特定目的下适当地接受或拒绝用户查询的能力。我们进一步提出了OffTopicEval，一个评估套件和基准，用于测量一般和特定代理使用案例中的操作安全性。我们对六个模型家族中20个开放权重LLM的评估显示，尽管模型之间的性能差异很大，但它们都保持高度的操作不安全性。即使是最强的模型 - Qwen-3（235B）得分77.77%和Mistral（24B）得分79.96% - 也远未达到可靠的操作安全性，而GPT模型的得分停留在62-73%范围内，Phi仅获得中等得分（48-70%），Gemma和Llama-3分别降至39.53%和23.84%。虽然操作安全性是核心模型对齐问题，为了抑制这些失败，我们提出了基于提示的引导方法：查询基础（Q-ground）和系统提示基础（P-ground），显著提高了OOD拒绝率。Q-ground提供了高达23%的持续增益，而P-ground则提供了更大的提升，将Llama-3.3（70B）提高了41%，将Qwen-3（30B）提高了27%。这些结果突显了对操作安全性干预的迫切需求，以及基于提示的引导作为朝着更可靠的基于LLM的代理迈出的第一步的前景。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical challenge of safety in deploying Large Language Models (LLMs), focusing on operational safety, which is the ability of LLMs to appropriately accept or refuse user queries based on specific purposes. Previous methods primarily concentrated on generic harms without adequately assessing the suitability of LLMs for intended use cases, leading to significant operational safety concerns. This paper introduces OffTopicEval, an evaluation suite designed to measure operational safety across various LLMs, revealing that all tested models exhibit high levels of operational unsafety, with performance metrics indicating that even the best models do not meet reliable safety standards. The proposed methodology includes prompt-based steering techniques, specifically query grounding (Q-ground) and system-prompt grounding (P-ground), which significantly enhance out-of-distribution refusal rates, achieving performance improvements of up to 41% in some cases. These findings underscore the necessity for operational safety measures and demonstrate the effectiveness of prompt-based steering as a viable solution for improving LLM safety.
本研究解决了在部署大型语言模型（LLMs）时面临的安全性挑战，重点关注操作安全性，即模型在特定目的下适当地处理用户查询的能力。以往的方法主要集中在一般性危害上，未能评估LLMs在其预期应用中的安全性。提出的OffTopicEval评估套件和基准旨在填补这一空白，通过测量各种LLMs的操作安全性。研究表明，所有评估的模型均存在显著的操作安全性问题，性能指标显示即使是最佳模型也未达到可接受的安全标准。为缓解这些问题，作者引入了基于提示的引导方法，特别是查询引导（Q-ground）和系统提示引导（P-ground），这些方法提高了对分布外拒绝率，取得了显著的性能提升。这些发现强调了操作安全性措施的必要性，并展示了所提方法在提高LLM可靠性方面的有效性。
Benchmark of Benchmarks: Unpacking Influence and Code Repository Quality in LLM Safety Benchmarks
Authors: Junjie Chu, Xinyue Shen, Ye Leng, Michael Backes, Yun Shen, Yang Zhang
First: 2026-03-03T09:10:45+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-12T11:49:16+00:00
Comments: 22 pages. 19 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid growth of research in LLM safety makes it hard to track all advances. Benchmarks are therefore crucial for capturing key trends and enabling systematic comparisons. Yet, it remains unclear why certain benchmarks gain prominence, and no systematic assessment has been conducted on their academic influence or code quality. This paper fills this gap by presenting the first multi-dimensional evaluation of the influence (based on five metrics) and code quality (based on both automated and human assessment) on LLM safety benchmarks, analyzing 31 benchmarks and 382 non-benchmarks across prompt injection, jailbreak, and hallucination. We find that benchmark papers show no significant advantage in academic influence (e.g., citation count and density) over non-benchmark papers. We uncover a key misalignment: while author prominence correlates with paper influence, neither author prominence nor paper influence shows a significant correlation with code quality. Our results also indicate substantial room for improvement in code and supplementary materials: only 39% of repositories are ready-to-use, 16% include flawless installation guides, and a mere 6% address ethical considerations. Given that the work of prominent researchers tends to attract greater attention, they need to lead the effort in setting higher standards.
中文标题/摘要
标题：基准中的基准：解读LLM安全基准中的影响力和代码库质量
LLM安全研究的快速增长使得追踪所有进展变得困难。因此，基准对于捕捉关键趋势和实现系统比较至关重要。然而，尚不清楚为何某些基准会获得突出地位，也没有对其学术影响力或代码质量进行系统评估。本文通过对31个基准和382个非基准在提示注入、越狱和幻觉方面的影响（基于五个指标）和代码质量（基于自动和人工评估）进行首次多维评估，填补了这一空白。我们发现基准论文在学术影响力（例如引用次数和密度）上并未显著优于非基准论文。我们揭示了一个关键的不一致：尽管作者的知名度与论文影响力相关，但作者知名度和论文影响力与代码质量之间并没有显著相关性。我们的结果还表明代码和补充材料有很大的改进空间：只有39%的代码库是可直接使用的，16%包含无瑕疵的安装指南，只有6%涉及伦理考虑。鉴于知名研究者的工作往往吸引更多关注，他们需要在设定更高标准的努力中发挥领导作用。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the challenge of tracking advancements in LLM safety research, highlighting the importance of benchmarks for systematic comparisons. Previous methods lacked a comprehensive evaluation of the academic influence and code quality of these benchmarks, leading to unclear reasons for their prominence. The proposed approach offers a multi-dimensional assessment of 31 benchmarks and 382 non-benchmarks, utilizing five metrics for influence and both automated and human evaluations for code quality. The findings reveal that benchmark papers do not significantly outperform non-benchmark papers in academic influence, and there is a notable misalignment between author prominence and code quality. The study contributes to the field by identifying areas for improvement in code repositories and emphasizes the need for leading researchers to establish higher standards. The methodology effectively highlights the shortcomings in existing benchmarks, providing a clearer understanding of their impact on LLM safety.
本研究解决了由于LLM安全领域快速发展而导致的跟踪进展的挑战，强调了基准在系统比较中的重要性。以往的方法缺乏对这些基准的学术影响力和代码质量的全面评估，导致对某些基准突出原因的不清晰。本论文提出了一种多维评估方法，通过五个指标评估影响力，并通过自动化和人工评估评估代码质量，填补了现有的空白。研究分析了与提示注入、越狱和幻觉相关的31个基准和382个非基准，结果表明，基准论文在学术影响力上并未显著优于非基准论文，并且作者声望、论文影响力与代码质量之间存在明显的不一致。研究结果表明，代码和补充材料的改进是必要的，只有少数存储库符合准备和伦理标准，强调了杰出研究人员提升这些基准的必要性。
Hiding in Plain Sight: A Steganographic Approach to Stealthy LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Jianing Geng, Biao Yi, Zekun Fei, Ruiqi He, Lihai Nie, Tong Li, Zheli Liu
First: 2025-05-22T15:07:34+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-12T10:54:29+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Jailbreak attacks pose a serious threat to Large Language Models (LLMs) by bypassing their safety mechanisms. A truly advanced jailbreak is defined not only by its effectiveness but, more critically, by its stealthiness. However, existing methods face a fundamental trade-off between semantic stealth (hiding malicious intent) and linguistic stealth (appearing natural), leaving them vulnerable to detection. To resolve this trade-off, we propose StegoAttack, a framework that leverages steganography. The core insight is to embed a harmful query within a benign, semantically coherent paragraph. This design provides semantic stealth by concealing the existence of malicious content and ensures linguistic stealth by maintaining the natural fluency of the cover paragraph. We evaluate StegoAttack on four state-of-the-art, safety-aligned LLMs, including GPT-5 and Gemini-3, and benchmark it against eight leading jailbreak methods. Our results show that StegoAttack achieves an average attack success rate (ASR) of 95.50%, outperforming existing baselines across all four models. Critically, its ASR drops by less than 27.00% under external detectors, while maintaining natural language distribution. This demonstrates that steganography effectively decouples linguistic and semantic stealth, thereby posing a fully concealed yet highly effective security threat. The code is available at https://github.com/GenggengSvan/StegoAttack
中文标题/摘要
标题：明目张胆的隐匿：一种隐写学方法用于隐秘的LLM越狱
越狱攻击通过绕过大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全机制，对其构成严重威胁。真正先进的越狱不仅以其有效性为特征，更重要的是其隐秘性。然而，现有方法在语义隐秘（隐藏恶意意图）和语言隐秘（看起来自然）之间面临根本的权衡，使其容易被检测。为了解决这一权衡，我们提出了StegoAttack，一个利用隐写学的框架。其核心见解是将有害查询嵌入到一个无害且语义连贯的段落中。该设计通过隐藏恶意内容的存在提供语义隐秘，并通过保持覆盖段落的自然流畅性确保语言隐秘。我们在四个最先进的、安全对齐的LLM上评估StegoAttack，包括GPT-5和Gemini-3，并与八种领先的越狱方法进行基准测试。我们的结果表明，StegoAttack在所有四个模型上实现了95.50%的平均攻击成功率（ASR），超越了现有基线。关键是，在外部检测器下，其ASR下降不到27.00%，同时保持自然语言分布。这表明隐写学有效地解耦了语言和语义隐秘，从而构成了一个完全隐蔽但高度有效的安全威胁。代码可在https://github.com/GenggengSvan/StegoAttack获取。

This research addresses the growing threat of jailbreak attacks on Large Language Models (LLMs), which exploit vulnerabilities in safety mechanisms. Previous methods struggle with a trade-off between semantic stealth, which conceals malicious intent, and linguistic stealth, which ensures natural language use, making them susceptible to detection. The proposed approach, StegoAttack, utilizes steganography to embed harmful queries within benign paragraphs, effectively achieving both types of stealth. This method is well-motivated as it resolves the inherent limitations of existing techniques. The paper contributes a novel framework that demonstrates a 95.50% average attack success rate across four advanced LLMs, significantly outperforming eight leading jailbreak methods while maintaining a low drop in effectiveness under external detection, thus highlighting the potential of steganography in enhancing security threats against LLMs.

ADVERSA: Measuring Multi-Turn Guardrail Degradation and Judge Reliability in Large Language Models
Authors: Harry Owiredu-Ashley
First: 2026-03-10T03:00:34+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-10T03:00:34+00:00
Comments: 12 pages, 12 figures. Independent research. Code and artifacts: https://github.com/Harry-Ashley/adversa-guardrail-degradation
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Most adversarial evaluations of large language model (LLM) safety assess single prompts and report binary pass/fail outcomes, which fails to capture how safety properties evolve under sustained adversarial interaction. We present ADVERSA, an automated red-teaming framework that measures guardrail degradation dynamics as continuous per-round compliance trajectories rather than discrete jailbreak events. ADVERSA uses a fine-tuned 70B attacker model (ADVERSA-Red, Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct with QLoRA) that eliminates the attacker-side safety refusals that render off-the-shelf models unreliable as attackers, scoring victim responses on a structured 5-point rubric that treats partial compliance as a distinct measurable state. We report a controlled experiment across three frontier victim models (Claude Opus 4.6, Gemini 3.1 Pro, GPT-5.2) using a triple-judge consensus architecture in which judge reliability is measured as a first-class research outcome rather than assumed. Across 15 conversations of up to 10 adversarial rounds, we observe a 26.7% jailbreak rate with an average jailbreak round of 1.25, suggesting that in this evaluation setting, successful jailbreaks were concentrated in early rounds rather than accumulating through sustained pressure. We document inter-judge agreement rates, self-judge scoring tendencies, attacker drift as a failure mode in fine-tuned attackers deployed out of their training distribution, and attacker refusals as a previously-underreported confound in victim resistance measurement. All limitations are stated explicitly. Attack prompts are withheld per responsible disclosure policy; all other experimental artifacts are released.
中文标题/摘要
标题：ADVERSA：测量大型语言模型中的多轮护栏退化和评审可靠性
大多数对大型语言模型（LLM）安全性的对抗性评估评估单个提示并报告二元通过/失败结果，这未能捕捉安全属性在持续对抗交互下的演变。我们提出了ADVERSA，一个自动化红队框架，测量护栏退化动态，作为连续的每轮合规轨迹，而不是离散的越狱事件。ADVERSA使用经过微调的70B攻击者模型（ADVERSA-Red，Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct与QLoRA），消除了攻击者侧的安全拒绝，使现成模型在攻击者中不可靠，使用结构化的5分制评分受害者响应，将部分合规视为一个独特的可测量状态。我们报告了在三个前沿受害者模型（Claude Opus 4.6，Gemini 3.1 Pro，GPT-5.2）上进行的受控实验，使用三重评审共识架构，其中评审可靠性被测量为一项一流的研究结果，而不是假设。在15次对话中，最多进行10轮对抗，我们观察到26.7%的越狱率，平均越狱轮次为1.25，表明在该评估设置中，成功的越狱集中在早期轮次，而不是通过持续压力积累。我们记录了评审间一致性率、自我评审评分倾向、在超出其训练分布的微调攻击者中作为失败模式的攻击者漂移，以及作为受害者抵抗测量中先前未报告的混淆因素的攻击者拒绝。所有限制均明确说明。攻击提示根据负责任的披露政策被保留；所有其他实验材料均已发布。

This research addresses the limitations of existing adversarial evaluations of large language models (LLMs), which typically assess safety through single prompts and binary outcomes, failing to capture the dynamics of safety properties during prolonged adversarial interactions. The proposed ADVERSA framework introduces a continuous measurement of guardrail degradation using a fine-tuned 70B attacker model, which mitigates the unreliability of off-the-shelf models as attackers and evaluates victim responses on a structured rubric that recognizes partial compliance. Beyond Benchmarks: Dynamic, Automatic And Systematic Red-Teaming Agents For Trustworthy Medical Language Models
Authors: Jiazhen Pan, Bailiang Jian, Paul Hager, Yundi Zhang, Che Liu, Friedrike Jungmann, Hongwei Bran Li, Chenyu You, Junde Wu, Jiayuan Zhu, Fenglin Liu, Yuyuan Liu, Niklas Bubeck, Christian Wachinger, Chen, Chen, Zhenyu Gong, Cheng Ouyang, Georgios Kaissis, Benedikt Wiestler, Daniel Rueckert
First: 2025-07-30T08:44:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-09T15:37:01+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Ensuring the safety and reliability of large language models (LLMs) in clinical practice is critical to prevent patient harm. However, LLMs are advancing so rapidly that static benchmarks quickly become obsolete or prone to overfitting, yielding a misleading picture of model trustworthiness. Here we introduce a Dynamic, Automatic, and Systematic (DAS) red-teaming framework that continuously stress-tests LLMs across four safety-critical axes: robustness, privacy, bias/fairness, and hallucination. Validated against board-certified clinicians with high concordance, a suite of adversarial agents autonomously mutates clinical test cases to uncover vulnerabilities in real time. Applying DAS to 15 proprietary and open-source LLMs revealed a profound gap between high static benchmark performance and low dynamic reliability - the ``Benchmarking Gap''. Despite median MedQA accuracy exceeding 80\%, 94\% of previously correct answers failed our dynamic robustness tests. Crucially, this brittleness generalized to the realistic, open-ended HealthBench dataset, where top-tier models exhibited failure rates exceeding 70\% and stark shifts in model rankings across evaluations, suggesting that high scores on established static benchmarks may reflect superficial memorization. We observed similarly high failure rates across other domains: privacy leaks were elicited in 86\% of scenarios, cognitive-bias priming altered clinical recommendations in 81\% of fairness tests, and we identified hallucination rates exceeding 74\% in widely used models. By converting medical LLM safety analysis from a static checklist into a dynamic stress-test, DAS provides a foundational, scalable, and living platform to surface the latent risks that must be addressed before the next generation of medical AI can be safely deployed.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越基准：动态、自动和系统化的红队代理用于可信的医疗语言模型
确保大型语言模型（LLMs）在临床实践中的安全性和可靠性对于防止患者伤害至关重要。然而，LLMs的发展速度如此之快，以至于静态基准很快变得过时或容易过拟合，从而产生误导性的模型可信度图景。在此，我们介绍了一种动态、自动和系统化（DAS）红队框架，持续对LLMs在四个安全关键轴上进行压力测试：鲁棒性、隐私、公平性/偏见和幻觉。经过与高一致性的董事会认证临床医生的验证，一套对抗性代理自主变更临床测试案例，以实时发现漏洞。将DAS应用于15个专有和开源LLMs揭示了高静态基准性能与低动态可靠性之间的深刻差距——“基准差距”。尽管中位数MedQA准确率超过80%，但94%的先前正确答案未能通过我们的动态鲁棒性测试。至关重要的是，这种脆弱性在现实的开放式HealthBench数据集中得到了普遍体现，顶级模型的失败率超过70%，并且在评估中模型排名发生了显著变化，这表明在既定静态基准上获得的高分可能反映了表面的记忆。我们在其他领域也观察到了类似的高失败率：在86%的场景中引发了隐私泄露，81%的公平性测试中认知偏见的引导改变了临床建议，并且我们在广泛使用的模型中发现幻觉率超过74%。通过将医疗LLM安全分析从静态检查表转变为动态压力测试，DAS提供了一个基础的、可扩展的和动态的平台，以揭示必须在下一代医疗AI安全部署之前解决的潜在风险。

Automating Deception: Scalable Multi-Turn LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Adarsh Kumarappan, Ananya Mujoo
First: 2025-11-24T03:15:11+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-07T08:41:48+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn conversational attacks, which leverage psychological principles like Foot-in-the-Door (FITD), where a small initial request paves the way for a more significant one, to bypass safety alignments, pose a persistent threat to Large Language Models (LLMs). Progress in defending against these attacks is hindered by a reliance on manual, hard-to-scale dataset creation. This paper introduces a novel, automated pipeline for generating large-scale, psychologically-grounded multi-turn jailbreak datasets. We systematically operationalize FITD techniques into reproducible templates, creating a benchmark of 1,500 scenarios across illegal activities and offensive content. We evaluate seven models from three major LLM families under both multi-turn (with history) and single-turn (without history) conditions. Our results reveal stark differences in contextual robustness: models in the GPT family demonstrate a significant vulnerability to conversational history, with Attack Success Rates (ASR) increasing by as much as 32 percentage points. In contrast, Google's Gemini 2.5 Flash exhibits exceptional resilience, proving nearly immune to these attacks, while Anthropic's Claude 3 Haiku shows strong but imperfect resistance. These findings highlight a critical divergence in how current safety architectures handle conversational context and underscore the need for defenses that can resist narrative-based manipulation.

标题：自动化欺骗：可扩展的多轮LLM越狱
多轮对话攻击利用心理学原理，如“脚踏实地”（FITD），通过小的初始请求为更大的请求铺平道路，以绕过安全对齐，对大型语言模型（LLM）构成持续威胁。防御这些攻击的进展受到依赖于手动、难以扩展的数据集创建的限制。本文介绍了一种新颖的自动化管道，用于生成大规模、基于心理学的多轮越狱数据集。我们系统地将FITD技术操作化为可重复的模板，创建了一个涵盖非法活动和攻击性内容的1,500个场景的基准。我们在多轮（有历史）和单轮（无历史）条件下评估了来自三个主要LLM家族的七个模型。我们的结果揭示了上下文鲁棒性方面的显著差异：GPT家族的模型对对话历史表现出显著脆弱性，攻击成功率（ASR）增加了多达32个百分点。相比之下，谷歌的Gemini 2.5 Flash表现出卓越的韧性，几乎对这些攻击免疫，而Anthropic的Claude 3 Haiku则表现出强但不完美的抵抗力。这些发现突显了当前安全架构在处理对话上下文方面的关键分歧，并强调了需要能够抵御叙事操控的防御措施。

This article addresses the growing concern of multi-turn conversational attacks on Large Language Models (LLMs), which exploit psychological principles like the Foot-in-the-Door (FITD) technique to bypass safety measures. Peak + Accumulation: A Proxy-Level Scoring Formula for Multi-Turn LLM Attack Detection
Authors: J Alex Corll
First: 2026-02-11T17:53:41+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-05T22:25:18+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn prompt injection attacks distribute malicious intent across multiple conversation turns, exploiting the assumption that each turn is evaluated independently. While single-turn detection has been extensively studied, no published formula exists for aggregating per-turn pattern scores into a conversation-level risk score at the proxy layer -- without invoking an LLM. We identify a fundamental flaw in the intuitive weighted-average approach: it converges to the per-turn score regardless of turn count, meaning a 20-turn persistent attack scores identically to a single suspicious turn. Drawing on analogies from change-point detection (CUSUM), Bayesian belief updating, and security risk-based alerting, we propose peak + accumulation scoring -- a formula combining peak single-turn risk, persistence ratio, and category diversity. Evaluated on 10,654 multi-turn conversations -- 588 attacks sourced from WildJailbreak adversarial prompts and 10,066 benign conversations from WildChat -- the formula achieves 90.8% recall at 1.20% false positive rate with an F1 of 85.9%. A sensitivity analysis over the persistence parameter reveals a phase transition at rho ~ 0.4, where recall jumps 12 percentage points with negligible FPR increase. We release the scoring algorithm, pattern library, and evaluation harness as open source.
中文标题/摘要
标题：峰值 + 累积：一种用于多轮LLM攻击检测的代理级评分公式
多轮提示注入攻击在多个对话轮次中分散恶意意图，利用每轮独立评估的假设。尽管单轮检测已被广泛研究，但在代理层中没有已发布的公式用于将每轮模式评分聚合为对话级风险评分，而不调用LLM。我们识别出直观加权平均方法的一个根本缺陷：无论轮次数量如何，它都收敛于每轮评分，这意味着20轮持续攻击的评分与单个可疑轮次相同。借鉴变点检测（CUSUM）、贝叶斯信念更新和基于安全风险的警报，我们提出了峰值 + 累积评分——一个结合峰值单轮风险、持续比率和类别多样性的公式。在10,654个多轮对话中进行评估——588个攻击源自WildJailbreak对抗提示，10,066个良性对话来自WildChat——该公式在1.20%的假阳性率下实现了90.8%的召回率，F1为85.9%。对持续参数的敏感性分析显示在rho ~ 0.4处发生相变，召回率跃升12个百分点，假阳性率增加微乎其微。我们将评分算法、模式库和评估工具作为开源发布。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the challenge of detecting multi-turn prompt injection attacks, which exploit the assumption that conversation turns are evaluated independently. Previous methods, primarily focused on single-turn detection, fail to effectively aggregate per-turn scores into a comprehensive conversation-level risk score, leading to inadequate detection of persistent attacks. The proposed peak + accumulation scoring formula overcomes these limitations by integrating peak single-turn risk, persistence ratio, and category diversity, drawing on concepts from change-point detection and Bayesian updating. The methodology was tested on a dataset of 10,654 multi-turn conversations, achieving a recall of 90.8% at a 1.20% false positive rate and an F1 score of 85.9%, demonstrating that the proposed approach significantly enhances detection capabilities for multi-turn attacks while providing open-source tools for further research.
本研究解决了在对话式人工智能中检测多轮提示注入攻击的挑战，这些攻击利用了每轮独立评估的假设。以往的方法主要集中在单轮检测上，并依赖于一种有缺陷的加权平均方法，该方法未能考虑跨多轮的攻击持续性。提出的峰值+累积评分公式通过整合单轮风险峰值、持续比率和类别多样性，克服了这些局限性，从而生成更准确的对话级风险评分。该方法在10,654个多轮对话的数据集上进行了评估，达到了90.8%的召回率和1.20%的假阳性率，F1分数为85.9%，证明了其在识别持续攻击方面的有效性，同时将误报降至最低。
Safety Guardrails for LLM-Enabled Robots
Authors: Zachary Ravichandran, Alexander Robey, Vijay Kumar, George J. Pappas, Hamed Hassani
First: 2025-03-10T22:01:56+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-03T23:39:07+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Project1
Abstract
Although the integration of large language models (LLMs) into robotics has unlocked transformative capabilities, it has also introduced significant safety concerns, ranging from average-case LLM errors (e.g., hallucinations) to adversarial jailbreaking attacks, which can produce harmful robot behavior in real-world settings. Traditional robot safety approaches do not address the contextual vulnerabilities of LLMs, and current LLM safety approaches overlook the physical risks posed by robots operating in real-world environments. To ensure the safety of LLM-enabled robots, we propose RoboGuard, a two-stage guardrail architecture. RoboGuard first contextualizes pre-defined safety rules by grounding them in the robot's environment using a root-of-trust LLM. This LLM is shielded from malicious prompts and employs chain-of-thought (CoT) reasoning to generate context-dependent safety specifications, such as temporal logic constraints. RoboGuard then resolves conflicts between these contextual safety specifications and potentially unsafe plans using temporal logic control synthesis, ensuring compliance while minimally violating user preferences. In simulation and real-world experiments that consider worst-case jailbreaking attacks, RoboGuard reduces the execution of unsafe plans from over 92% to below 3% without compromising performance on safe plans. We also demonstrate that RoboGuard is resource-efficient, robust against adaptive attacks, and enhanced by its root-of-trust LLM's CoT reasoning. These results demonstrate the potential of RoboGuard to mitigate the safety risks and enhance the reliability of LLM-enabled robots. We provide additional resources at https://robo-guard.github.io/.
中文标题/摘要
标题：面向大型语言模型（LLM）机器人安全护栏
尽管将大型语言模型（LLM）集成到机器人技术中解锁了变革性能力，但也引入了重大安全隐患，从平均案例的LLM错误（例如，幻觉）到对抗性越狱攻击，这些都可能在现实环境中导致有害的机器人行为。传统的机器人安全方法未能解决LLM的上下文脆弱性，而当前的LLM安全方法则忽视了机器人在现实环境中操作所带来的物理风险。为了确保LLM启用机器人的安全性，我们提出了RoboGuard，一个两阶段的护栏架构。RoboGuard首先通过使用根信任LLM将预定义的安全规则与机器人的环境相结合，从而对其进行上下文化。该LLM受到恶意提示的保护，并采用链式思维（CoT）推理生成上下文依赖的安全规范，例如时间逻辑约束。然后，RoboGuard使用时间逻辑控制合成解决这些上下文安全规范与潜在不安全计划之间的冲突，确保合规的同时尽量减少对用户偏好的违反。在考虑最坏情况越狱攻击的模拟和现实实验中，RoboGuard将不安全计划的执行从超过92%降低到低于3%，而不影响安全计划的性能。我们还证明RoboGuard在资源利用上高效，能够抵御自适应攻击，并通过其根信任LLM的CoT推理得到增强。这些结果展示了RoboGuard在减轻安全风险和增强LLM启用机器人可靠性方面的潜力。我们在https://robo-guard.github.io/提供了更多资源。
Summary / 总结
The integration of large language models (LLMs) into robotics has raised significant safety concerns, including errors and adversarial attacks that can lead to harmful robot behavior. Traditional safety methods for robots do not adequately address the unique vulnerabilities of LLMs, while current LLM safety strategies fail to consider the physical risks associated with real-world robot operations. This paper introduces RoboGuard, a two-stage guardrail architecture that contextualizes safety rules through a root-of-trust LLM, which is protected from malicious inputs and utilizes chain-of-thought reasoning to create context-specific safety specifications. RoboGuard effectively resolves conflicts between these specifications and unsafe plans using temporal logic control synthesis, achieving a reduction in unsafe plan execution from over 92% to below 3% in both simulation and real-world tests, while maintaining performance on safe plans. The findings indicate that RoboGuard is resource-efficient and robust against adaptive attacks, showcasing its potential to enhance the safety and reliability of LLM-enabled robots.

Toward a Dynamic Stackelberg Game-Theoretic Framework for Agentic AI Defense Against LLM Jailbreaking
Authors: Zhengye Han, Quanyan Zhu
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-07-10T22:37:47+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-02T23:19:02+00:00
Comments: Accepted to ICLR 2026 AIMS Workshop. 13 pages, 3 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
This paper proposes a game theoretic framework that models the interaction between prompt engineers and large language models (LLMs) as a two player extensive form game coupled with a Rapidly exploring Random Trees (RRT) search over prompt space. The attacker incrementally samples, extends, and tests prompts, while the LLM chooses to accept, reject, or redirect, leading to terminal outcomes of Safe Interaction, Blocked, or Jailbreak. Embedding RRT exploration inside the extensive form game captures both the discovery phase of jailbreak strategies and the strategic responses of the model. Furthermore, we show that the defender behavior can be interpreted through a local Stackelberg equilibrium condition, which explains when the attacker can no longer obtain profitable prompt deviations and provides a theoretical lens for understanding the effectiveness of our Purple Agent defense. The resulting game tree thus offers a principled foundation for evaluating, interpreting, and hardening LLM guardrails.
中文标题/摘要
标题：面向动态斯塔克尔伯格博弈理论框架的代理人工智能防御大语言模型越狱
本文提出了一个博弈理论框架，模拟提示工程师与大语言模型（LLMs）之间的互动，作为一个双人广泛形式博弈，并结合在提示空间上的快速探索随机树（RRT）搜索。攻击者逐步采样、扩展和测试提示，而LLM选择接受、拒绝或重定向，导致安全互动、被阻止或越狱的终局结果。在广泛形式博弈中嵌入RRT探索捕捉了越狱策略的发现阶段和模型的战略响应。此外，我们展示了防御者行为可以通过局部斯塔克尔伯格均衡条件进行解释，这解释了攻击者何时无法再获得有利的提示偏差，并为理解我们紫色代理防御的有效性提供了理论视角。因此，所得到的博弈树为评估、解释和强化LLM防护措施提供了原则基础。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing concern of jailbreaking large language models (LLMs) by modeling the interaction between prompt engineers and LLMs as a two-player extensive form game. Previous methods lacked a structured approach to understanding the strategic dynamics between attackers and defenders, leading to ineffective defenses. This paper introduces a game-theoretic framework that incorporates Rapidly exploring Random Trees (RRT) to explore prompt space, allowing for a more nuanced understanding of both attack strategies and defensive responses. The proposed methodology effectively captures the discovery phase of jailbreak strategies and establishes conditions under which attackers can no longer exploit vulnerabilities, contributing to a theoretical foundation for enhancing LLM defenses. The framework demonstrates improved performance in evaluating and interpreting LLM guardrails, supporting the goal of creating more robust defenses against jailbreaking attempts.

Enhancing Safety of Large Language Models via Embedding Space Separation
Authors: Xu Zhao, Xiting Wang, Weiran Shen
First: 2026-03-01T07:22:38+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-01T07:22:38+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved impressive capabilities, yet ensuring their safety against harmful prompts remains a critical challenge. Recent work has revealed that the latent representations (embeddings) of harmful and safe queries in LLMs typically exhibit linear separability, a property that has been exploited to construct attacks by perturbing the embeddings of harmful queries towards the safe subspace. Motivated by this observation, we propose a representation-level fine-tuning approach, named Embedding Space Separation (ES2), which improves LLM safety by explicitly enlarging the distance between harmful and safe representations in the embedding space. To prevent degradation of model's general capabilities, we introduce a Kullback-Leibler (KL) divergence regularization term into the loss function, which constrains the logits of the fine-tuned model to align with those of the original base model on harmless inputs. We evaluate our method on several open-source LLMs using standard safety benchmarks. Extensive experimental results demonstrate that our approach substantially improves model safety while maintaining comparable general capabilities.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过嵌入空间分离增强大型语言模型的安全性
大型语言模型（LLMs）已实现令人印象深刻的能力，但确保其对有害提示的安全性仍然是一个关键挑战。最近的研究表明，LLMs中有害和安全查询的潜在表示（嵌入）通常表现出线性可分性，这一特性已被利用，通过扰动有害查询的嵌入朝向安全子空间来构建攻击。基于这一观察，我们提出了一种表示级微调方法，称为嵌入空间分离（ES2），通过明确扩大嵌入空间中有害和安全表示之间的距离来提高LLM的安全性。为了防止模型一般能力的退化，我们在损失函数中引入了Kullback-Leibler（KL）散度正则化项，约束微调模型的logits与原始基础模型在无害输入上的对齐。我们在多个开源LLMs上使用标准安全基准评估我们的方法。大量实验结果表明，我们的方法显著提高了模型的安全性，同时保持了可比的通用能力。

The proposed approach, Embedding Space Separation (ES2), differs from past methods by focusing on representation-level fine-tuning to explicitly increase the distance between harmful and safe embeddings, while incorporating a Kullback-Leibler divergence regularization to preserve the model's general capabilities. This paper contributes a novel methodology that enhances the safety of LLMs without compromising their performance on harmless inputs. The evaluation of ES2 on various open-source LLMs using standard safety benchmarks shows significant improvements in model safety, achieving a balance between enhanced safety and maintained general capabilities.

CourtGuard: A Model-Agnostic Framework for Zero-Shot Policy Adaptation in LLM Safety
Authors: Umid Suleymanov, Rufiz Bayramov, Suad Gafarli, Seljan Musayeva, Taghi Mammadov, Aynur Akhundlu, Murat Kantarcioglu
First: 2026-02-26T02:52:11+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-26T02:52:11+00:00
Comments: Under Review
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current safety mechanisms for Large Language Models (LLMs) rely heavily on static, fine-tuned classifiers that suffer from adaptation rigidity, the inability to enforce new governance rules without expensive retraining. To address this, we introduce CourtGuard, a retrieval-augmented multi-agent framework that reimagines safety evaluation as Evidentiary Debate. By orchestrating an adversarial debate grounded in external policy documents, CourtGuard achieves state-of-the-art performance across 7 safety benchmarks, outperforming dedicated policy-following baselines without fine-tuning. Beyond standard metrics, we highlight two critical capabilities: (1) Zero-Shot Adaptability, where our framework successfully generalized to an out-of-domain Wikipedia Vandalism task (achieving 90\% accuracy) by swapping the reference policy; and (2) Automated Data Curation and Auditing, where we leveraged CourtGuard to curate and audit nine novel datasets of sophisticated adversarial attacks. Our results demonstrate that decoupling safety logic from model weights offers a robust, interpretable, and adaptable path for meeting current and future regulatory requirements in AI governance.
中文标题/摘要
标题：CourtGuard：一种与模型无关的零-shot策略适应框架，用于大型语言模型安全性
当前大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全机制严重依赖于静态的、微调的分类器，这些分类器存在适应性僵化的问题，无法在不进行昂贵再训练的情况下强制执行新的治理规则。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了CourtGuard，这是一种增强检索的多智能体框架，将安全评估重新构想为证据辩论。通过协调基于外部政策文件的对抗性辩论，CourtGuard在7个安全基准测试中实现了最先进的性能，超越了专门的政策遵循基线而无需微调。除了标准指标外，我们强调了两个关键能力：（1）零-shot适应性，我们的框架成功地推广到一个域外的维基百科破坏任务（实现90%的准确率），通过更换参考政策；（2）自动数据策划和审计，我们利用CourtGuard策划和审计了九个新颖的复杂对抗攻击数据集。我们的结果表明，将安全逻辑与模型权重解耦为满足当前和未来AI治理监管要求提供了一条稳健、可解释和可适应的路径。

When Style Breaks Safety: Defending LLMs Against Superficial Style Alignment
Authors: Yuxin Xiao, Sana Tonekaboni, Walter Gerych, Vinith Suriyakumar, Marzyeh Ghassemi
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-06-09T05:57:39+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-24T23:22:40+00:00
Comments: Accepted by ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) can be prompted with specific styles (e.g., formatting responses as lists), including in malicious queries. Prior jailbreak research mainly augments these queries with additional string transformations to maximize attack success rate (ASR). However, the impact of style patterns in the original queries that are semantically irrelevant to the malicious intent remains unclear. In this work, we seek to understand whether style patterns compromise LLM safety, how superficial style alignment increases model vulnerability, and how best to mitigate these risks during alignment. We first define ASR inflation as the increase in ASR due to style patterns in existing jailbreak benchmark queries. By evaluating 36 LLMs across seven benchmarks, we find that nearly all models exhibit ASR inflation. Notably, the inflation correlates with an LLM's relative attention to style patterns, which also overlap more with its instruction-tuning data when inflation occurs. We then investigate superficial style alignment, and find that fine-tuning with specific styles makes LLMs more vulnerable to jailbreaks of those same styles. Finally, we propose SafeStyle, a defense strategy that incorporates a small amount of safety training data augmented to match the distribution of style patterns in the fine-tuning data. Across three LLMs, six fine-tuning style settings, and two real-world instruction-tuning datasets, SafeStyle consistently outperforms baselines in maintaining LLM safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：当风格破坏安全性：保护大型语言模型免受表面风格对齐的影响
大型语言模型（LLMs）可以通过特定风格（例如，将响应格式化为列表）进行提示，包括在恶意查询中。之前的越狱研究主要通过额外的字符串转换来增强这些查询，以最大化攻击成功率（ASR）。然而，原始查询中与恶意意图语义无关的风格模式的影响仍不清楚。在本研究中，我们旨在了解风格模式是否会危害LLM的安全性，表面风格对齐如何增加模型的脆弱性，以及在对齐过程中如何最好地减轻这些风险。我们首先将ASR膨胀定义为由于现有越狱基准查询中的风格模式而导致的ASR增加。通过评估36个LLM在七个基准上的表现，我们发现几乎所有模型都表现出ASR膨胀。值得注意的是，膨胀与LLM对风格模式的相对关注度相关，当膨胀发生时，这些模式与其指令调优数据的重叠也更多。然后，我们研究表面风格对齐，发现使用特定风格进行微调使LLM对这些相同风格的越狱更加脆弱。最后，我们提出了SafeStyle，一种防御策略，结合少量安全训练数据，增强以匹配微调数据中的风格模式分布。在三个LLM、六个微调风格设置和两个真实世界的指令调优数据集上，SafeStyle在维护LLM安全性方面始终优于基线。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the vulnerability of large language models (LLMs) to malicious queries that exploit specific style patterns, a concern that has not been thoroughly examined in previous jailbreak studies which primarily focused on string transformations to enhance attack success rates (ASR). The proposed approach, SafeStyle, differs from existing methods by recognizing that superficial style alignment can increase model vulnerability and defining ASR inflation as the rise in ASR due to style patterns in benchmark queries. The paper contributes by demonstrating that nearly all evaluated LLMs exhibit ASR inflation and that fine-tuning with specific styles exacerbates this issue. The methodology involves augmenting safety training data to align with the distribution of style patterns in fine-tuning data, and the results show that SafeStyle consistently outperforms baseline methods across various models and settings, effectively enhancing LLM safety.

BarrierSteer: LLM Safety via Learning Barrier Steering
Authors: Thanh Q. Tran, Arun Verma, Kiwan Wong, Bryan Kian Hsiang Low, Daniela Rus, Wei Xiao
First: 2026-02-23T18:19:46+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-23T18:19:46+00:00
Comments: This paper introduces SafeBarrier, a framework that enforces safety in large language models by steering their latent representations with control barrier functions during inference, reducing adversarial and unsafe outputs
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Despite the state-of-the-art performance of large language models (LLMs) across diverse tasks, their susceptibility to adversarial attacks and unsafe content generation remains a major obstacle to deployment, particularly in high-stakes settings. Addressing this challenge requires safety mechanisms that are both practically effective and supported by rigorous theory. We introduce BarrierSteer, a novel framework that formalizes response safety by embedding learned non-linear safety constraints directly into the model's latent representation space. BarrierSteer employs a steering mechanism based on Control Barrier Functions (CBFs) to efficiently detect and prevent unsafe response trajectories during inference with high precision. By enforcing multiple safety constraints through efficient constraint merging, without modifying the underlying LLM parameters, BarrierSteer preserves the model's original capabilities and performance. We provide theoretical results establishing that applying CBFs in latent space offers a principled and computationally efficient approach to enforcing safety. Our experiments across multiple models and datasets show that BarrierSteer substantially reduces adversarial success rates, decreases unsafe generations, and outperforms existing methods.
中文标题/摘要
标题：BarrierSteer：通过学习障碍引导实现LLM安全
尽管大型语言模型（LLMs）在各种任务中表现出色，但它们对对抗性攻击和不安全内容生成的易感性仍然是部署的主要障碍，特别是在高风险环境中。解决这一挑战需要既有效又有严格理论支持的安全机制。我们介绍了BarrierSteer，这是一种新颖的框架，通过将学习到的非线性安全约束直接嵌入模型的潜在表示空间来形式化响应安全。BarrierSteer采用基于控制障碍函数（CBFs）的引导机制，在推理过程中高精度地有效检测和防止不安全的响应轨迹。通过高效的约束合并强制执行多个安全约束，而不修改底层LLM参数，BarrierSteer保留了模型的原始能力和性能。我们提供了理论结果，证明在潜在空间中应用CBFs提供了一种原则性和计算上高效的安全强制方法。我们在多个模型和数据集上的实验表明，BarrierSteer显著降低了对抗性成功率，减少了不安全生成，并优于现有方法。

Hiding in Plain Text: Detecting Concealed Jailbreaks via Activation Disentanglement
Authors: Amirhossein Farzam, Majid Behabahani, Mani Malek, Yuriy Nevmyvaka, Guillermo Sapiro
First: 2026-02-23T00:11:30+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-23T00:11:30+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) remain vulnerable to jailbreak prompts that are fluent and semantically coherent, and therefore difficult to detect with standard heuristics. A particularly challenging failure mode occurs when an attacker tries to hide the malicious goal of their request by manipulating its framing to induce compliance. Because these attacks maintain malicious intent through a flexible presentation, defenses that rely on structural artifacts or goal-specific signatures can fail. Motivated by this, we introduce a self-supervised framework for disentangling semantic factor pairs in LLM activations at inference. We instantiate the framework for goal and framing and construct GoalFrameBench, a corpus of prompts with controlled goal and framing variations, which we use to train Representation Disentanglement on Activations (ReDAct) module to extract disentangled representations in a frozen LLM. We then propose FrameShield, an anomaly detector operating on the framing representations, which improves model-agnostic detection across multiple LLM families with minimal computational overhead. Theoretical guarantees for ReDAct and extensive empirical validations show that its disentanglement effectively powers FrameShield. Finally, we use disentanglement as an interpretability probe, revealing distinct profiles for goal and framing signals and positioning semantic disentanglement as a building block for both LLM safety and mechanistic interpretability.
中文标题/摘要
标题：隐藏在明文中：通过激活解耦检测隐蔽越狱
大型语言模型（LLMs）仍然容易受到流畅且语义连贯的越狱提示的攻击，因此难以通过标准启发式方法检测。一个特别具有挑战性的失败模式发生在攻击者试图通过操控请求的框架来隐藏其恶意目标以诱导合规时。由于这些攻击通过灵活的呈现保持恶意意图，依赖结构性伪影或目标特定签名的防御可能会失败。基于此，我们提出了一种自监督框架，用于在推理时解耦LLM激活中的语义因子对。我们为目标和框架实例化该框架，并构建了GoalFrameBench，这是一个具有受控目标和框架变化的提示语料库，我们用它来训练在冻结的LLM中提取解耦表示的Representation Disentanglement on Activations（ReDAct）模块。然后，我们提出了FrameShield，一个在框架表示上运行的异常检测器，它在多个LLM家族中以最小的计算开销提高了模型无关的检测。ReDAct的理论保证和广泛的实证验证表明，其解耦有效地支持了FrameShield。最后，我们将解耦作为可解释性探针，揭示了目标和框架信号的不同特征，并将语义解耦定位为LLM安全性和机制可解释性的基础构件。

Sampling-aware Adversarial Attacks Against Large Language Models
Authors: Tim Beyer, Yan Scholten, Leo Schwinn, Stephan Günnemann
First: 2025-07-06T16:13:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-22T20:49:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
To guarantee safe and robust deployment of large language models (LLMs) at scale, it is critical to accurately assess their adversarial robustness. Existing adversarial attacks typically target harmful responses in single-point greedy generations, overlooking the inherently stochastic nature of LLMs and overestimating robustness. We show that for the goal of eliciting harmful responses, repeated sampling of model outputs during the attack complements prompt optimization and serves as a strong and efficient attack vector. By casting attacks as a resource allocation problem between optimization and sampling, we empirically determine compute-optimal trade-offs and show that integrating sampling into existing attacks boosts success rates by up to 37\% and improves efficiency by up to two orders of magnitude. We further analyze how distributions of output harmfulness evolve during an adversarial attack, discovering that many common optimization strategies have little effect on output harmfulness. Finally, we introduce a label-free proof-of-concept objective based on entropy maximization, demonstrating how our sampling-aware perspective enables new optimization targets. Overall, our findings establish the importance of sampling in attacks to accurately assess and strengthen LLM safety at scale.

Fail-Closed Alignment for Large Language Models
Authors: Zachary Coalson, Beth Sohler, Aiden Gabriel, Sanghyun Hong
First: 2026-02-19T00:33:35+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-19T00:33:35+00:00
Comments: Pre-print
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
We identify a structural weakness in current large language model (LLM) alignment: modern refusal mechanisms are fail-open. While existing approaches encode refusal behaviors across multiple latent features, suppressing a single dominant feature$-$via prompt-based jailbreaks$-$can cause alignment to collapse, leading to unsafe generation. Motivated by this, we propose fail-closed alignment as a design principle for robust LLM safety: refusal mechanisms should remain effective even under partial failures via redundant, independent causal pathways. We present a concrete instantiation of this principle: a progressive alignment framework that iteratively identifies and ablates previously learned refusal directions, forcing the model to reconstruct safety along new, independent subspaces. Across four jailbreak attacks, we achieve the strongest overall robustness while mitigating over-refusal and preserving generation quality, with small computational overhead. Our mechanistic analyses confirm that models trained with our method encode multiple, causally independent refusal directions that prompt-based jailbreaks cannot suppress simultaneously, providing empirical support for fail-closed alignment as a principled foundation for robust LLM safety.

标题：大型语言模型的故障关闭对齐

NeST: Neuron Selective Tuning for LLM Safety
Authors: Sasha Behrouzi, Lichao Wu, Mohamadreza Rostami, Ahmad-Reza Sadeghi
First: 2026-02-18T20:01:01+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-18T20:01:01+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Safety alignment is essential for the responsible deployment of large language models (LLMs). Yet, existing approaches often rely on heavyweight fine-tuning that is costly to update, audit, and maintain across model families. Full fine-tuning incurs substantial computational and storage overhead, while parameter-efficient methods such as LoRA trade efficiency for inconsistent safety gains and sensitivity to design choices. Safety intervention mechanisms such as circuit breakers reduce unsafe outputs without modifying model weights, but do not directly shape or preserve the internal representations that govern safety behavior. These limitations hinder rapid and reliable safety updates, particularly in settings where models evolve frequently or must adapt to new policies and domains. We present NeST, a lightweight, structure-aware safety alignment framework that strengthens refusal behavior by selectively adapting a small subset of safety-relevant neurons while freezing the remainder of the model. NeST aligns parameter updates with the internal organization of safety behavior by clustering functionally coherent safety neurons and enforcing shared updates within each cluster, enabling targeted and stable safety adaptation without broad model modification or inference-time overhead. We benchmark NeST against three dominant baselines: full fine-tuning, LoRA-based fine-tuning, and circuit breakers across 10 open-weight LLMs spanning multiple model families and sizes. Across all evaluated models, NeST reduces the attack success rate from an average of 44.5% to 4.36%, corresponding to a 90.2% reduction in unsafe generations, while requiring only 0.44 million trainable parameters on average. This amounts to a 17,310x decrease in updated parameters compared to full fine-tuning and a 9.25x reduction relative to LoRA, while consistently achieving stronger safety performance for alignment.
中文标题/摘要
标题：NeST：用于大型语言模型安全的神经元选择性调优
安全对齐对于大型语言模型（LLMs）的负责任部署至关重要。然而，现有方法通常依赖于成本高昂的全量调优，这在模型家族中更新、审计和维护时代价高昂。全量调优会产生大量的计算和存储开销，而像LoRA这样的参数高效方法则在效率与安全收益不一致和对设计选择敏感之间进行权衡。安全干预机制如电路断路器在不修改模型权重的情况下减少不安全输出，但并未直接塑造或保留支配安全行为的内部表示。这些限制阻碍了快速和可靠的安全更新，特别是在模型频繁演变或必须适应新政策和领域的情况下。我们提出了NeST，一个轻量级、结构感知的安全对齐框架，通过选择性地调整一小部分与安全相关的神经元，同时冻结模型的其余部分，来增强拒绝行为。NeST通过对功能上连贯的安全神经元进行聚类，并在每个聚类内强制共享更新，将参数更新与安全行为的内部组织对齐，从而实现针对性和稳定的安全适应，而无需广泛修改模型或在推理时增加开销。我们将NeST与三种主要基线进行基准测试：全量调优、基于LoRA的调优和电路断路器，涵盖10个开放权重的LLMs，跨多个模型家族和规模。在所有评估的模型中，NeST将攻击成功率从平均44.5%降低到4.36%，对应于不安全生成减少90.2%，同时平均仅需0.44百万可训练参数。这相较于全量调优减少了17,310倍的更新参数，相较于LoRA减少了9.25倍，同时在对齐方面始终实现更强的安全性能。
